The Mystery of "Death": There is No Scientific Evidence for the Immortality of the Soul 73

— Special

Dr. Alexis Carrel, an American biologist, speculates that within the next three hundred years, rejuvenation techniques may advance to the point where science can determine that "death" is eternally a mystery. At the same time, he warned the public that artificially delaying "death" and allowing many useless people to remain in the world is more harmful than "death" itself. This is in line with the ancient Chinese saying that "an old person who does not die is a thief."

The doctor said at a recent discussion on "The Mystery of Death" at the New York Medical College! "If human life suddenly increases to a hundred years, then civilization will not be able to bear the economic burden of a population dominated by the elderly. Today's customs and institutions of civilization contain an order, that is, many weak, chronically ill, and stupid people in society can be cleared away with the help of "death."

The doctor did not believe in any of the scientific evidence that has been developed for the immortality of the soul. He said: "Hundreds of millions of people now believe in the immortality of the soul. This belief belongs to the realm of religion and philosophy, but not to the realm of experimental science. Spiritualists claim that the soul lives on after death and has been proven. However, the activity of the mind, as we know it, is an image of a living body, and after the organs disintegrate, it will never manifest itself. There is currently no scientific evidence for the theory that spirituality or part of spirituality still exists after death, but no one has the right to say that this existence is impossible."

The doctor then cited the potential immortality of cells. As long as Colonel Lindbergh's recently invented method is used, all the organs of a dead animal can still grow and maintain the circulation of artificial blood. The doctor himself took a heart dug out of a chicken's stomach in the Rockefeller Institute, immediately placed it in a glass tube, and used scientific methods to maintain its vitality. It has been beating vigorously for twenty-four years.

The doctor finally mentioned resurrection and rejuvenation, saying: "If a dead person is revived too late, then although the person is resurrected, they have no soul. Once, a woman regained life nine minutes after being legally dead, but her limbs were numb and her behavior was like an animal. The activity of the mind probably disappeared before the body died, and after death, it will never manifest itself."

"Spiritualists claim that the soul lives on after death and has been proven, and there is experimental evidence. We cannot deny the importance of the facts on which this speculation is based. However, their interpretation of the experimental results does not seem correct. Spiritualists forget that there is clairvoyance that can perceive things in the past and the future, so the spiritual principles that exist after death and the phenomena revealed by clairvoyance are exactly one and two, and two and one. It is impossible to distinguish between them."

"One of the forces that resist "death" is to seek physiological factors that can determine the limit of life. There are many centenarians in the world now, which shows that our bodies contain greater potential than we realize. In addition to heredity, certain health regimens, certain foods, or certain life-extending mental attitudes are all important conditions. The research on these conditions is still in its infancy today, but many meaningful facts have already been discovered." The doctor then cited the experience of raising mice in the Rockefeller Institute as evidence. Some foods can increase body size, and the resulting mouse pups are larger than usual and can also reduce the possibility of contracting pneumonia, but they cannot prolong life. Other foods can reduce body size, and in the first month, they can also increase the death rate, but they can indeed prolong life. This result makes people believe that the proper use of food and health regimens can prolong human life.

The doctor also said: "Dry cells also have latent life. Mr. Li Boxuzi once connected a semi-dry organism to a guinea pig, and it was able to revive and secrete glands again."

The doctor then made playful speculations about this ideal, thinking that we can put the creatures of the world in a state of suspended animation for a long time, and prolong the "death" of a limited number of individuals for a long time. He said: "Although this matter is very vague now, it is one of the four major possibilities. In the future, it may be possible to store some individuals for a long time, keeping them neither alive nor dead, and then restore them to normal life for a certain time. Maybe we can use this method to make them live for hundreds of years. Although this sounds absurd, we must know that today's utopia is tomorrow's reality."

"Because the time recorded by the clock passes irreversibly within the bodies of various creatures, it also records the order, so it is an incredible thing for us to conquer "death." The average life expectancy of people has now increased significantly, and the maximum limit of life may be greatly extended in the future. In the future, there may be sudden unexpected new inventions that will open up new possibilities for rejuvenation. The duel between people and "death" may not be beautiful even after victory, because artificially delaying the "death" of many people is more harmful than "death" itself. "Death" is neither a disaster nor a blessing. "Death" is not an accident from the outside, but a part of ourselves, which is inevitable and an indispensable condition for life." The doctor's remarks can eliminate many people's misconceptions about greed for life and fear of death, and break the dream of becoming an immortal.

International Business Telecommunications 74

Reuters Special Business News, January 13

Gold and Silver: The price of gold in London today is one hundred and forty shillings and eleven pence, the same as the previous closing price.

British Silver: The London silver market is stable today. The spot price is twenty and a half pence, the same as the closing price on Friday. Speculators sold, and India bought.

American Silver: The Montreux silver market is stable. The March futures price is listed as 46.30 - 50.

Exchange Rates

British and American: The London foreign exchange market was mixed this morning. Europe still expects the dollar to depreciate again soon, while London believes that although President Roosevelt has the power to lower the currency price, he will never use it lightly unless something unexpected happens. The two factions have different opinions, so the dollar price continues to fluctuate. The British-American exchange rate was four dollars, ninety-six cents, and six two five at half past ten, which was eight seven five lower than yesterday's closing price in the United States and the United Kingdom. It rose half a point at eleven o'clock and continued to rise six two five an hour later. Around two o'clock in the afternoon, the market price was firm, rising six two five higher than the opening price, and the price was four dollars, ninety-seven cents, and two five.

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened lower due to the drop in Liverpool prices and the instability of the market. The opening fell six pounds, and there was still a downward trend.

British Cotton: Liverpool cotton production prices plummeted due to the unstable situation in the United States. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the January futures price was five pence and seventy-eight, a drop of thirteen pounds.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was quiet today. The price rose slowly because Australia sold a large number of wheat to the East. The number of weekly shipments did not affect the wheat market because although the number of shipments to the United Kingdom increased, European purchases were also considerable and could be offset. Liverpool's reserves are now gradually decreasing. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the March futures price rose one two five to six shillings and seven pence two five.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market was weak due to the good wheat production conditions, the closing of long positions, and short selling. The May futures price was 100.375, half a point lower than the closing price on Saturday. The situation in the miscellaneous grain market was the same as that of wheat.

Rubber

New York: New York rubber opened slightly higher because the London telegram was good and the demand from the industry was also good. Prices were stable in the morning.

The Sino-Japanese Negotiations in Dagu Started with the Arrest of Smugglers. The Japanese Side Has Put Forward Six Demands. 78

Tianjin communication. Japanese military officers from inside and outside the pass gathered in Tianjin to hold a conference on the situation in North China, which has led to a sudden increase in tension in recent days. The two issues that are being used as pretexts are: First, the misunderstanding and conflict between Chinese and Japanese military police at Chaoyangmen in Beiping; Second, the Twenty-ninth Army stationed at Dagu Port, which the Japanese side accused of insulting Japanese businessmen and tearing up the Japanese flag. The Tanggu area has always been a formal military defense area. Since the conflict between the Thirty-second Army and the Zhao Lei Department of the Pseudo-Hebei Security Force, the defense area has been ceded. There are no regular troops stationed in Tanggu. Only a company from the Liu Jinshan Brigade of the 132nd Division of the Twenty-ninth Army is stationed in Dagu. On January 2, several merchants who were smuggling Japanese goods were found by the garrison troops when they were secretly entering the country. The garrison troops, together with the police chief of the local police station, pursued the smugglers. The merchants fled into the Oshimagumi and Daishimagumi, two Japanese firms in West Dagu. The military police stopped at the door and asked the firms to hand over the criminals. The Japanese in the two firms refused. Chen Yongli, a Chinese hired by the Oshimagumi, even relied on his power to insult the military police. He was arrested by his mother Chen Wu and handed over to the Public Security Bureau for punishment. On the morning of the 3rd, Oshima Kihachiro, the owner of the Oshimagumi, crossed the river and forcibly entered the military defense area, wanting to ask the garrison to release Chen Yongli and his mother. The troops refused to allow him to approach the shore and instructed him to negotiate with the police station. On the 4th, Watanabe Mihiko, a Japanese resident in Dongdazhan, was also suspected of smuggling goods and drugs. He was searched by the troops. Watanabe was dissatisfied and escaped, and then reported to Kataoka, the chief of the Tanggu Japanese Police Station Branch. Together with the military police, Bohe asked to see the garrison officer of the Twenty-ninth Army. The army said that all responsibility rested with the police station and should be handled by the police station. There was no need for the army to have direct talks, so they were not received. This also caused dissatisfaction from the Japanese side. On the 6th, people from the police station, together with troops from the Twenty-ninth Army, escorted Chen Yongli, a Chinese from the Oshimagumi who had been arrested, to the Daishimagumi to identify the criminals. After the Daishimagumi left, it suddenly tore up the Japanese flag hanging outside the door and smashed the doors and windows, etc., falsely accusing the military police of doing it. The Oshimagumi also imitated Daishimagumi's trick of planting evidence, deliberately messing up the miscellaneous items in the room and tearing down the Japanese flag. As a result, the Tianjin Japanese Army and the Japanese Consulate General clamored, believing that the Twenty-ninth Army had insulted the Japanese side. On the evening of the 6th, in addition to sending Chen Dongsheng, a member of the Hebei Provincial Government stationed in Tianjin, to negotiate with the Japanese side and promising to thoroughly investigate and handle the matter, the Pingjin Garrison Headquarters also ordered Lu Nansheng, a member of the department, to come to Tianjin and go to Dagu to investigate with Onozaki, the judicial director of the Japanese Consulate General, and Police Officer Hara. On the same day, Consul General Kawakoshi sent a letter to the Tianjin office of the Hebei Provincial Government based on the reports of the owners of the two firms, Daishimagumi and Oshimagumi, and the Twenty-ninth Army separately sent protests. The wording was still mild and could have been resolved peacefully. Chen Dongsheng went to Baoding that night to report to Song Zheyuan the process of contacting the Japanese side. However, on the morning of the 7th, Ono, the director of the investigation sent to Dagu, and Police Officer Hara returned to Tianjin and reported to Kawakoshi. At the same time, the Japanese Army adopted a persistent attitude, refusing to understand and supporting the serious protest of the consulate. Song, upon hearing the news in Baoding, urgently ordered Xiao Zhenying to negotiate. Xiao met with Commander Tada and Chief of Staff Nagami, but their attitudes were very tough and negotiations could not continue. On the afternoon of the 9th, the Japanese side re-submitted a protest in the name of Consul General Kawakoshi. In addition to listing eight facts in the original text, there were six demands attached: 1. The chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government and the commander of the Twenty-ninth Army must formally apologize to the Japanese side in writing. 2. The directly responsible persons of the Dagu Garrison Army and the Public Security Bureau Branch must be dismissed. 3. The arrested criminals must be severely punished. 4. Compensation for damages. 5. The headquarters of the Twenty-ninth Army and the Hebei Provincial Government must order their subordinates not to insult the Japanese side again in the future. 6. Guarantee that such incidents will not happen again in the future. The letter of protest was still sent to the headquarters of the Twenty-ninth Army and the Tianjin office of the Hebei Provincial Government. Currently, the Dagu garrison company commander has been automatically replaced, and the chief of the Dagu Police Station, Zhang, has fled in fear of crime. The Japanese side's responsibility for the negotiations seems to have been transferred from the consulate to the garrison army. What will be expressed in the future will depend on the decision of the Tianjin military officer conference. (11th)

Representatives from the Two Guangdong Factions Welcome Hu Hanmin Back to the Country. Representatives from Various Southwest Agencies Go to Singapore to Meet Hu. Zhang Renmin and Pan Yizhi of the Gui Faction Arrive in Guangdong to Await His Arrival. 79

Chao-Shan: Vagrant Japanese Roaming Unrestrainedly, Openly Robbing Private Cargo Ships in Broad Daylight; South China Puppet Autonomous Government is Brewing 80

Shantou Correspondence: Since December 1st of last year, after the Chao-Shan Anti-Smuggling Bureau unified anti-smuggling powers, various tax-collecting merchants and companies were no longer allowed to send inspectors to investigate and harass travelers and returning overseas Chinese. Since then, they have gained many conveniences. Upon landing, after the customs officers inspected their luggage, and after being inspected by the tax police of the Anti-Smuggling Bureau, they could move their luggage into hotels or take boats and cars to their hometowns in the interior. Currently, the Chao-Shan Anti-Smuggling Bureau has a battalion of armed tax police, with five anti-smuggling vessels distributed in key locations on land and water for patrol. Six inspection zones and twenty-one checkpoints have been established in various counties under Chaozhou's jurisdiction. They focus on investigating and seizing heavily taxed goods such as smuggled oil, rice, beans, various textiles, matches, and alcohol, in order to maintain the income from various taxes. Since the anti-smuggling operation began, it has achieved great results. A large amount of smuggled goods has been seized from shops and residents along the waterways and roads. At the same time, many major international negotiations have also taken place. However, the income of the agricultural and miscellaneous tax bureau has gradually improved. At the end of last month, Chinese merchants purchased 70,000 to 80,000 bags of taxable beans from Shanghai, and the lifeless Shantou North-South Trade Grain Merchants and Oil Merchants have seen a revival. The smuggled goods seized by the Anti-Smuggling Bureau used to be sent to Shantou for processing. However, after the incident of vagrant Japanese robbing cargo ships on the evening of the 17th of last month, all seizures in various counties are now handled locally. For serious cases involving political implications, they will be escorted to Guangdong for punishment on the 4th of this month.

At 4 PM on the 4th of this month, a smuggling rice boat with more than 100 bags of rice and beans was intercepted in the Chao-Yang sea area and towed back to the Shantou Deji Foreign Firm pier. As it was being unloaded into the warehouse, the Anti-Smuggling Bureau sent four inspectors to supervise. Towards evening, more than ten vagrant Japanese suddenly appeared, armed with knives and axes, first beating the guarding inspectors and cutting the ship's cable with axes, intending to rob and transport the cargo away. The inspectors resisted desperately and reported to the Anti-Smuggling Bureau, which sent 50 armed tax police to temporarily guard and impose martial law on the seaside, dispersing a group of armed men. Traffic on nearby roads was temporarily cut off. Finally, the rice and beans in the ship were completely unloaded into the warehouse overnight, and martial law was lifted the next morning. Some vagrant Japanese approached Xiao Sheng, the director of the Anti-Smuggling Bureau, falsely claiming that the rice and beans belonged to them and making many unreasonable demands. Xiao went to see Li Yukun, the chief of staff of the Eastern District Public Office, and reported to Mayor Li Yuanhe, saying that if the vagrant Japanese continued to act so unrestrainedly, unexpected events might occur. That night, he telegraphed the details to the province, requesting Li Han-hun to return to Shantou as soon as possible to take charge. In addition, there has recently been a brewing of a South China puppet autonomous government in Chao-Shan. A fake Plum Blossom Party organization was discovered in Songkou Township. In the past two months, an increasing number of vagrant Japanese have been sneaking into the interior from Taiwan and Xiamen. They are active in the lower levels of society, forming ×× societies, and enticing poor farmers, workers, and the unemployed. They set up hospitals and pharmacies in various fairs, secretly engaging in high-profit businesses. It is reported that the coastal terrain of Chaoyang, Dahao, Aotou, and Haimen has all been photographed. Even the key point of entering Shantou from Chaozhou at Donghu Bogong Ridge has been surveyed by the vagrant Japanese, despite the people's resistance. The Guangdong General Headquarters believes that the vagrant Japanese have ulterior motives and secretly telegraphed the Chao-Mei county magistrates and defense forces to pay attention to the comings and goings of pedestrians, and issued a notice stating that no foreign nationals are allowed to arbitrarily photograph scenery or steal terrain without a passport and permission from military and political authorities.

The Ping-Han Railway Bureau Takes Over the Dao-Qing Railway: Changed to a Branch Line, Reducing Scope for Reorganization; Clearing Foreign Debt Set to Be Completed Within Fifteen Years 81

Hankou Correspondence: Railway Minister Zhang Jia , at the beginning of his tenure, advocated merging the Dao-Qing Railway into the Ping-Han Railway, reducing its scope, and engaging in reorganization. Later, he sent Zou Anzhong, deputy director of the Ping-Han Railway Bureau, to Jiaozuo to take over. Now it has been completed. Mr. Zou returned to Hankou from Jiaozuo today and reported the details to Beijing by telegram. The Dao-Qing Railway starts from the Luo River and ends at Daokou, with a total length of more than 170 kilometers. Because the route is too short, and the only product along the line is the coal produced by the Jiaozuo Zhongfu Company, there is a lack of large-scale products for transportation. Therefore, the annual revenue of the road is only about 1.8 to 1.9 million yuan. After deducting expenses of more than 1.6 million, there is only a surplus of about 200,000 yuan. However, the foreign debt owed to the British merchant bank group is as high as 1.6 million yuan, and the surplus is not enough to pay the interest. The future is indeed worrying. Mr. Zhang Jiawei believes that reorganizing railway administration must start with clearing foreign debt, and clearing foreign debt requires the road to reduce its organization and save expenses. Therefore, it was decided to merge the Ping-Han Railway Bureau for management. After gathering Chen Yanjiong, director of the Ping-Han Railway Administration Bureau, and Zou Anzhong, deputy director, in Beijing, a method was agreed upon and changed to the Dao-Qing branch line. At the end of last year, the Railway Department issued a clear order to Hankou and sent Zou to Jiaozuo to take over. Zou immediately ordered the five departments of the bureau to send staff to go together. They departed north from Hankou on December 31 and arrived in Jiaozuo on January 2 of this year. At that time, a small number of Dao-Qing employees intended to instigate a disturbance and resist the order. After Zou gathered them for a lecture, explaining the Ministry's intention to merge the Dao-Qing Railway, it was for the purpose of reorganizing the railway and unifying management. The employees deeply understood the righteousness and happily complied. The takeover began on the 2nd and was completed by the 8th. The Dao-Qing Railway Bureau originally had five departments: Transportation, Engineering, Mechanical, General Affairs, and Accounting, as well as a Railway Police Department. After merging into the Ping-Han Railway, the directors of the General Affairs and Accounting departments were first dismissed, and the directors of the Transportation, Engineering, and Mechanical departments, as well as the chief of the Police Department, were changed to section chiefs. The remaining staff were assessed and selectively retained. Those who were dismissed were given severance pay ranging from one to three months, and a bonus of one month, depending on their seniority. The workers and railway police remained as before, without any reductions. Although accounting was also merged, revenue and expenditure were still separated to facilitate debt settlement. It is reported that the Ping-Han Railway Bureau's plan for reorganizing the Dao-Qing branch line in the future, such as adjusting transportation, increasing and decreasing freight rates, and purchasing vehicles and cultivating roads, has been determined. Attention will be paid to the item of clearing foreign debt. Generally, after the merger, revenue can be increased by 400,000 yuan, and expenses can be reduced by 200,000 yuan, with an annual surplus of more than 800,000 yuan. It is hoped that interest on foreign debt can be waived and gradually paid off within fifteen years. When Mr. Zou took over, he was ordered by the Ministry to also serve as a representative for negotiating foreign debt. He held two resolutions with Mr. Bell, the representative of the British Zhongfu Company, in Jiaozuo as a preliminary negotiation, and the opinions have become closer. Bell will come to Hankou within days to make detailed negotiations, and Mr. Woodrow, the chairman of the company, will also come to China from England to preside over the negotiations. After a method is agreed upon in Hankou, the Ping-Han Railway Bureau will submit it to the Ministry of Railways for approval and implementation. (12th)

Due to the agricultural disaster and poor harvest this year, the rice shop owners in Suzhou have received few rental payments. Now that the rent riots have ceased, and after the village district chiefs mediated, the rice shop owners have agreed to reduce the quality and amount of rent by discretion. To accommodate the farmers, the rice shop owners have decided to work together and establish public warehouses throughout the villages to collect rents. With the end of the lunar year approaching, the provincial government needs funds urgently, so he sternly ordered all grain households to quickly go to the county and pay the land price tax.

Old Man Uses Clever Tricks to Deceive Pharmacy

At around 8 AM on the morning of the 12th, an old man suddenly came to the store to buy medicine, claiming to be from Xuzhou and selling horses in Changzhou, buying medicine along the way. He then put the medicine into the empty box and added cod liver oil, hemostatic single medicine, cotton, etc., and tied it up with a mat bag. As the store owner was opening the account to wait for him to pay and deliver the goods, the old man suddenly said that he had not brought the money and needed to go get it, so he would delay picking up the goods. After saying that, he turned and left. The store owner became suspicious and inspected the wrapped medicine box. Who knew that the medicine in the box had disappeared without a trace, leaving only ten large pieces of hemp cake? The other large cigarette boxes were also full of shredded paper and messy ropes. So, he sent his partners to search everywhere. Soon, they saw the old man at the train station, getting on the train and putting the medicine into a bag. They immediately grabbed him. The old man knew that his scam had been exposed and quickly returned the original items, cupped his hands, and apologized. The store partner then took the items and returned. Ningbo

Resolution of the Hefeng Factory Shutdown Tide

Workers at the Hefeng Yarn Factory in Jiangdong, claiming that the factory was shutting down due to the excuse of prolonged rain and difficulty in collecting raw materials, which made it difficult to make a living, petitioned the Party and government authorities to seek justice. After the Yinxian Party Department and the Yinxian Government summoned representatives from both labor and management for mediation on the afternoon of the 10th, the result was a decision to operate at least seven days before the 23rd of this month. The dates will be decided and announced by the factory. During the overall shutdown period, the factory will lend each worker eight wages. The wages lent before and after will be deducted by three wages per month in February, March, and April of this year. If there is a reduction in working hours in February, March, and April, one wage will be deducted from the lent wages, and two wages will be handled as usual. Both parties were satisfied and dispersed.

Education Broadcasting Special Edition

Public Speaking on the National Language Subject: How to Read 82

— Xia Genzun, Compilation Director of Kaiming Bookstore

The day before yesterday, I gave a speech to middle school students on the topic of "What to Read." Today's speech can be seen as a continuation of the previous one, with the topic being "How to Read." The previous speech, "What to Read," was about the types of reading materials. Today's speech, "How to Read," is about the methods of reading.

"How to Read," like "What to Read," is an old question, and many people have said various things about it in the past. What I am talking about today does not contain any new ideas or methods that have not been expressed by predecessors. Today's speech is for middle school students, and I only hope that my words will be suitable for middle school students.

When I talked about "What to Read" last time, I divided the scope of reading into three aspects. The first is books related to one's profession, the second is reference books, and the third is books for cultivating personal interests. The profession of middle school students is learning middle school courses, and middle school textbooks belong to the first category. When studying schoolwork, other books are needed for reference, which are reference books and belong to the second category. Selecting some books that suit one's personal interests or are related to self-cultivation to read outside of class is the third category. Today, when talking about "How to Read," I still want to talk about it based on these three aspects.

First, let's talk about the first category, books related to your profession, which are textbooks. There are two types of textbooks on your desk: one with a rigorous system and one without a rigorous system. Subjects such as mathematics, physics, chemistry, geography, history, botany, zoology, etc., all have certain chapters and a certain order, which is a systematic approach. Subjects such as national language readers and English readers do not have a rigorous system. An essay by Han Yu can be included in the first volume of junior high school national language, or it can be included in the second volume of senior high school national language. A biography of Benjamin Franklin can be placed in the third volume of junior high school English or the second volume of senior high school English. If you pay attention to the textbooks you are using, you will already know this situation. This situation is not accidental and can be said to be related to the nature of the subject. Those with a rigorous system belong to the general so-called sciences, while subjects like national language and English focus on language and writing. Except for grammar books and rhetoric books, the general so-called readers and textbooks are all used as models and tools for practice, so they do not have a rigorous system themselves. Since textbooks have this distinction, the methods of reading should also be different.

If we separate reading into two types, general science textbooks should focus on reading, while language and literature textbooks should focus on reciting. General science textbooks are also written in language, but our learning goal is not the language itself. For example, when we learn geography or chemistry, what we should pay attention to is the subject matter recorded in the geography and chemistry books. These items are originally recorded in language, except for diagrams and charts, but we do not need to memorize and ponder them specifically through language. We only need to obtain the content from the language. As for language subjects, it is different. When we read an article in the national language textbook—let's say it is a record by Han Yu—at this time, we should not only know who Han Yu is and understand the content of this record, but we should also have other goals, such as the structure of the article, the style of the sentences, the methods of description and expression, etc., all of which must be studied. If you read Han Yu's record and only know that there was such a painting at the time and that Han Yu wrote such an article, then it is equivalent to not having studied this article as a national language lesson. When we read the story of Washington cutting down the cherry tree in the English textbook, the purpose is not to know why Washington cut down the cherry tree and what happened later, but to use this story as material for learning English and to acquire various rules of English. Therefore, the two words "reading" can be used separately. General science textbooks should understand their content and should not waste effort on language. Just read them well. Subjects such as national language and English are language subjects and should focus more on form. Just reading is not enough; you should study them well.

Whether it is reading or reciting, you should not relax when it comes to textbooks, because this is formal schoolwork and your professional work. If you have any doubts, you should look up the dictionary. If you have any questions, you should look up the books. This is the so-called reference book. Reference books are prepared for diligent people, because in order to refer to something, you must first have items or questions to refer to. These items or questions will only arise from people who read carefully in all aspects. I have already talked about this reason in the previous speech. Those who have heard it should still be able to remember it. I won't say much more. Now let me talk about some things that should be paid attention to when reading reference books.

First, I advise you to temporarily determine the scope of reference and not abandon the items or questions you want to refer to. When we look up a dictionary, we are generally satisfied when we find the word or allusion we want to look up and will not be distracted by the dictionary. However, if it is a reference book other than a dictionary, one may often stray far away if one is not careful. For example, you read "Peach Blossom Spring" and go to read a message about Thomas More's Utopia as a reference book for the item "Utopian thought," which is correct, but you must temporarily remember that what you want to refer to is "Utopian thought," not other items. Don't let your mind wander to very distant places because you read a message about Thomas More's Utopia. Thomas More advocated art and was a social thinker. If you are not careful, you may forget what you read about "Peach Blossom Spring" and circle around ideas such as social thought and art, turning from aspect A to aspect B, and then turning from aspect B to aspect C, resulting in a chaotic mind. When we talk to friends, we often stray far from the topic and forget what we were just talking about. This is very similar to abandoning the original topic because of reading reference books. People who understand the art of speaking will often remind their opponents in this situation to bring the conversation back to the matter at hand. You should pay the same attention when reading reference books and should not be distracted by aspects that are not directly related to the topic you want to refer to.

Second, I advise you to take advantage of the convenience of reference to pay attention to the general nature and content of general books. Apart from checking dictionaries and flipping through magazines, so-called reference books are usually independent books. Each book has its own nature, content, and organizational style. Since you have the opportunity to see a certain book for reference, it is not difficult to learn something about the book. In middle school, you have various tasks to do, and there is very little time for extracurricular reading. However, some books are indispensable for knowledge and future application. For example, we do not read the "Twenty-Four Histories" and the "Thirteen Classics" in middle school, but we should know what the "Twenty-Four Histories" and the "Thirteen Classics" are. We are not Christians and do not need to read the Bible, but we should know the general content of the New and Old Testaments. If you are reading a history lesson and want to know more details about the topic of "Emperor Wu of Han expanding the territory," you can flip through the "Records of the Grand Historian" or the "Book of Han." At this time, you will probably flip through the table of contents first. When you flip through the table of contents, you will definitely see titles such as "Annals," "Hereditary Houses," "Biographies," "Tables," and "Treatises." This is the organizational structure of the "Records of the Grand Historian" or the "Book of Han." After reading one chapter of the "Annals of Emperor Wu," or several sections of the entire chapter, and then looking at these table of contents, you will have a relationship with the "Records of the Grand Historian" or the "Book of Han." You can understand what kind of books the "Records of the Grand Historian" and the "Book of Han" are in general. To give another example, you hear the words "Theory of Evolution" from a teacher of botany or zoology. If you want to know more details about this topic, you can go to the library to find a book to read. Suppose you find a "Outline of the Theory of Evolution" by Chen Jianshan, you can first read the preface to see what aspects this book talks about, and then check the table of contents to see what items are inside. What you want to refer to now may only be one section or one chapter of it, but the comprehensive knowledge of this whole book is very useful to you. If you pay attention at any time, you can acquire the comprehensive and general knowledge of many books in a year. Over time, you will know what is in those books. To check those items, you should find which police and flipping through will be very convenient. (To be continued)

The Ningjing Stranded on Chenjia Island; 5 Miles from Jiujiang; Telegraph Old Ning Shao to Tow for Rescue 87

In recent months, there has been very little cargo shipped downstream on the Yangtze River. Recently, as the end of the lunar year approaches, business groups must ship goods to Shanghai as soon as possible for economic settlement. Therefore, the Ningjing Wheel of the Ning Shao Company, returning from Hankou to Shanghai, was fully loaded with more than 20,000 pieces of tobacco, cotton, grain, and other goods, making it one of the largest shipments downstream carried by the ship. It was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai today to unload at the warehouse. Unexpectedly, since the beginning of this month, the water level of the Yangtze River has been sharply receding. Around the 10th, the drop was even greater, falling more than two feet a day. On the 12th of this month, the highest water mark in Jiujiang was no more than 16 feet. In Wuhu, the lowest point was 13 feet. The Ningjing Wheel has a load capacity of 1,693 tons and is a new ship of the Ning Shao Company. The hull is 250 feet 6 inches long, 37 feet 4 inches wide, and 19 feet 6 inches deep. The draft of the empty ship is 16 feet 7 inches, and it is more than 17 feet after loading. At 8:00 PM on the 12th, when the ship arrived at Chenjia Island, 5 miles downstream from Jiujiang, it suddenly ran aground. At that time, because the hull was stuck in shallow sand and the water receded with a heavy load, the captain repeatedly reversed the engine but could not get out of the shallows. He had to telegraph Shanghai for help and instructions. Yesterday morning, after discussions at the Shanghai company, they immediately telegraphed the Jiujiang branch to quickly send barges to Chenjia Island to unload the cargo from the Ningjing's cabins. If the Ningjing could be rescued immediately, the cargo would be loaded back into the ship and carried to Shanghai. Barging has been underway since yesterday afternoon. When reporters inquired at the company, a Mr. Chen in charge said that the reason for the Ningjing's grounding had not yet been reported by the captain, but it was mostly due to shallow water. Now that the cargo has been barged, it is hoped that the weight of the ship will be reduced, and it may float to the surface of the river. Today, the Old Ning Shao ship is passing through Chenjia Island, and the company has telegraphed the ship, ordering it to go and tow for rescue.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables Hubei Provincial Government Requesting Reduction of National Silk Business Tax 97

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday cabled the Hubei Provincial Government in Wuchang, which read: To the Hubei Provincial Government in Wuchang, we have received a letter from the Silk Industry Association on the 11th of this month stating that based on a letter from Supervisor Wang Yansong, the Hankou Huahua Company branch had forwarded a letter from the Hankou Silk Industry Association stating that the Hubei Finance Department intends to separately levy taxes on stores that also operate in silk, cloth, and wool based on the tax rates for the three industries starting in March of the 25th year, and to classify wool-like fabrics and rayon textiles as foreign goods and increase tax rates, etc. If implemented, this would have a significant impact on the future of the silk industry. Please find a way to maintain the current situation, etc. Now we are forwarding the situation and request that you strive to uphold the principles of the matter (omitted). The Business Tax Law, as resolved by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government, stipulates in its fourth provision that taxes should be levied at a rate of 2 to 10 per thousand of the total business income, and that the minimum rate for business income as a business tax rate is 2 per thousand of the total income. Furthermore, the Executive Yuan's circular to all provincial and municipal governments in the 19th year of the Republic stated that the Ministry of Industry reported that silk, in our country, is nothing less than a special national product and needs protection. It is proposed that the Executive Yuan instruct all provinces that the business tax on silk should be in accordance with daily necessities, and the tax rate should not exceed 2 per thousand in order to maintain it. In addition to instructing the Ministry of Industry to present the matter, it is stated that silk is a special national product and needs protection, and its use is also for the daily necessities of the common people. Please instruct all provinces to collect business tax, and the tax rate should not exceed 2 per thousand in order to maintain it. It should be approved and handled accordingly. Please order the Ministry of Finance and all provincial and municipal governments to comply and handle it accordingly. This order, etc., is printed, distributed, and ordered to be complied with. Therefore, the silk business tax should be levied at the lowest tax rate of 2 per thousand, which is a general case approved by the Executive Yuan. All provinces should be consistent. As for the mixing of rayon in silk, its main purpose is to resist imported goods. The Ministry of Industry revised the provisional standards for domestic goods in June of the 23rd year of the Republic, dividing them into seven grades. Those with Chinese capital, Chinese management, Chinese labor, mostly using domestic raw materials, and a small part using foreign raw materials are considered second-grade domestic goods. Those mostly using foreign raw materials are considered fourth-grade domestic goods. If the use of rayon is taxed as foreign goods, then the mixing of foreign cotton in cotton yarn and the mixing of foreign wheat in flour can all be referred to as foreign goods. This violates the standards set by the Ministry and is not in accordance with the fairness of the matter. Based on the above reasons, we hereby submit this telegram to your government for review. Please uphold the current tax rate, as it is in the public interest. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully.

Post Offices in Various Places Will Issue Social Savings Gift Certificates 114

Since the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications promulgated the rules for social telegrams, social interactions have become extremely convenient. In order to develop the telegraph business, a type of social postal savings gift certificate will be issued. This type of gift certificate will be sold by the National Postal Administration Savings and Remittance Bureau and first-class post offices throughout the country. Senders of social telegrams may attach gift certificates to the recipients, and the remittance fee for the gift certificates will be waived. The face value of these gift certificates ranges from two yuan to twenty yuan, and the certificates are divided into red and plain two types, which the sender can freely specify. Holders of social gift certificates can exchange them for legal currency at the local post office or postal machinery office at full value. The Shen Shi News Agency reporter learned from the bureau that before the issuance of social savings gift certificates, the rules for social telegrams will also be modified to suit the circumstances of the issuance of gift certificates. It is said that this measure will be implemented in March.

It Snowed in the City Yesterday 115

The weather in the city has been unstable with alternating periods of cold and warm for several days. Although it has rained occasionally, it still feels dry, causing many citizens to suffer from sore throats. At the same time, pests are rampant in the fields in the suburbs, which will affect this year's agricultural activities. Therefore, farmers in general are praying for auspicious snow to avoid disasters. Until about 4 p.m. yesterday, the weather suddenly changed dramatically, with the cold wind piercing to the bone and the overcast sky densely covered. Shortly after, there was light rain. After about half an hour, it turned into snow pellets, but it stopped soon. Then, snowflakes began to fly, dancing wildly in the sky. However, because the rain had not subsided, it melted as it fell. After about twenty minutes, the snow stopped, but the rain did not stop. At about 8:30 p.m., it snowed again, and it was denser than during the day, about two points high, but it still melted. It became sparse at about 10 p.m. and then stopped. However, the weather and wind direction have changed completely. We may hope for a heavy snowfall during the day.

The Case of Thirteen Native Banks Suing the Continental Bank for Confirmation of Bond-Receipt Contracts - The Plaintiff Refutes the Defendant's Response in Six Points - The First Special Court Scheduled a Continued Hearing Today to Summon Both Parties 119

The Continental Bank previously entered into a contract with 13 native banks, including Huafeng, Runfeng, Yuanfeng, Zhentai, Changshun, Yisheng, Fuchang, Yuzhong, Wanmao, Huatong, Demao, Hengmao, and Zhengkang, to receive a total of 1.75 million yuan in Central and Southern Bank banknotes. Each bank deposited 40% cash as collateral, and the Continental Bank paid interest on the collateral at a weekly rate of 6.5%. However, since the Ministry of Finance promulgated the Unified Currency System Issuance Order on November 4 of last year, the Continental Bank has used this as an excuse to demand that the banks cancel the bond-receipt contracts they had signed. After the banks sent representatives Ma Wenxiang, Liu Ximeng, Yin Huanzhi, and others to negotiate with Ye Fuxiao, the manager of the Continental Bank, without success, they retained attorney Zhan Jifeng to file a lawsuit against the Continental Bank in the First Special District Court to confirm the contract and pay interest. A hearing was held once, as reported in the previous newspaper. It is now learned that the Continental Bank submitted a written response to the court a few days ago, listing eight reasons. The court then sent the response to the plaintiff, and the plaintiff's attorney, Zhan Jifeng, filed a reply refuting each point, stating that upon examining the reasons given by the defendant, they may appear reasonable on the surface, but upon actual investigation, there is no evidence to support them. Therefore, a summary of the reply is provided below:

The Ministry of Finance's implementation of the Unified Currency System on November 4 of last year only prohibited the use of hard silver ingots. It did not prohibit the use of banknotes specially issued by private banks. Not only was it not prohibited, but it was also clearly stated in the announcement that all silver coins, such as those exchanged for the aforementioned specially issued banknotes, would also be allowed to circulate. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance's order to unify the currency system had no impact on the current status of the plaintiff's promotion of Central and Southern banknotes. The matter is very clear. Unexpectedly, the defendant used this order to cancel the plaintiff's rights and interests with far-fetched reasons. Regardless of law or reason, it is difficult to allow. As for the so-called Central and Southern banknotes that have been printed but not issued cannot be implemented, and the banknotes that have already been issued will also be gradually withdrawn, the former should be increased in issuance depending on the bank's own needs. If the banknotes currently issued are sufficient for use, then even without an explicit order from the Ministry of Finance, there is no need to increase the issuance. However, the defendant listed it as one of the reasons for terminating the contract, which lacks basis. The latter, the so-called gradual withdrawal, the meaning of the word "gradual" has a broad boundary. Has the currency already begun to be gradually withdrawn? Are the withdrawals the unmarked notes promoted by the plaintiff? The defendant did not make a clear statement. Moreover, more than two months have passed since the bank received the order. If the statement of gradual withdrawal is not false, then a large amount should have been withdrawn during this long period. Why not declare the exact amount in the defense to prove their statement? According to the Civil Procedure Law, a party seeking a judgment from the court that is favorable to them must bear the burden of proof. Now, the defendant is making empty claims without presenting any evidence. This is one reason why the contract cannot be terminated. The reasons stated in the second and third points of the defendant's defense are nothing more than the fact that since the Ministry of Finance issued the order to unify the currency system, the plaintiff can no longer continue to perform the contract. Without hearing or knowing the reasons, the defendant cannot say that the reasons are reasonable. The fact is that on the plaintiff's side, there is absolutely no situation of being unable to continue to perform. The reason why they cannot continue to perform is actually because the defendant is taking advantage of the opportunity and not following the fourth and fifth articles of the contract in order. Instead, they blame the plaintiff for not being able to fulfill their mission. Inverting right and wrong, nothing is more extreme. The government's implementation of the unified currency policy only prohibits the use of hard silver ingots, as mentioned above. At the same time, it does not prohibit the use of Central and Southern banknotes. In other words, as long as the Central and Southern banknotes are not prohibited, the rights and obligations under the contract between the two parties will naturally continue for one day. The defendant's so-called purpose of the contract and the continuity of the work are eliminated due to the law, which is all sophistry and not factual. This is two reason why the contract cannot be terminated. In the third point of the defendant's defense, it is stated that the exchange coupons received by the plaintiff are being continuously promoted by the defendant to make them fully circulate on the market. The plaintiff has searched the contract but has not found the words "continuously". Since there is no such term, it can be seen that it was fabricated by the defendant out of thin air. The plaintiff's responsibility is only to exchange the unmarked coupons whenever they are returned (see the defendant's defense statement). The plaintiff has fulfilled this obligation for many years. The defendant said that although the plaintiff wants to receive coupons, there are no coupons to receive, and although they want to promote them, there are no coupons to issue. It is important to know that after the contract was signed, the plaintiff immediately received all the unmarked coupons as per the contract. The statements in the defense are all irrelevant. The reason why the defendant is fabricating stories is nothing more than to know that they are wrong and intend to confuse the public. This is three reason why the contract cannot be terminated. In the fourth point of the defendant's defense, it is said that the benefits enjoyed are very large, and then it is said that the plaintiff is妄think of profits without labor, as if the plaintiff has actually obtained some kind of luxury. Knowing that the contract between the two parties, as the defendant said, one party must fulfill its obligations before it can demand the payment of rights. On the plaintiff's side, the obligations fulfilled in accordance with the contract cannot be said to be not important. For example, in Article 6 of the contract, if the defendant exchanges the unmarked coupons, if the plaintiff does not perform in accordance with the provisions of Articles 4 and 5 of the contract, then the cash advanced by the defendant shall be calculated in full according to the Shanghai market discount rate, plus 4.5 yuan (that is, at least 9% interest per month per thousand yuan). If the daily discount rate increases, it shall be increased accordingly. Also, as in Article 4 of the contract, if the plaintiff sends someone to the defendant to exchange the unmarked coupons, all responsibilities such as theft and loss during the round trip shall be borne by the plaintiff. Think about it, according to the contract, the responsibility borne by the plaintiff is so great, and the security deposit only has 40%, which can earn a few percent interest per year, while 60% does not calculate interest. The plaintiff's responsibility is so great, and the interest earned is so small. However, in the defendant's defense, they still exaggerate and say that the plaintiff has received generous benefits. Examining their intention, it is nothing more than because the termination of the contract has no legal basis, so they specially lay out the benefits in order to win the sympathy of the society and avoid criticism. How can a contract that has been legally established be protected by law and allowed to be arbitrarily terminated? This is four reason why the contract cannot be terminated. The fifth and sixth points of the defendant's defense are either a repetition of the meaning or have little relevance to this case, so there is no need to say more. As for the seventh point, the so-called reduction in currency circulation is not enough to compensate for the loss. If that is the case, then they should welcome the plaintiff for their inability to circulate it, so why take the excuse to terminate the contract? The wording is contradictory and self-defeating. This is five reason why the contract cannot be terminated. The eighth point of the defendant's defense refers to the plaintiff's claim for interest on late payment as an unearned profit, which is really inappropriate. It is stipulated in the Civil Code that if a payment has a definite deadline, the debtor shall be liable for late payment from the expiration date of the deadline. The law has clear provisions, so why allow a strong defense? In this case, the security deposit paid by the plaintiff to the defendant, its 40% annual interest, should be paid at the end of each year in accordance with Article 3 of the contract. Then, from the end of the 24th year of the Republic of China, the defendant should bear the interest on late payment. What is the benefit without labor? This is six reason why the contract cannot be terminated. This case is related to the financial community's receipt of bonds, which involves a large amount of money, so the money industry in this city attaches great importance to it. The First Special Court is scheduled to continue the trial this afternoon by Judge Huang Daxi. At that time, the representatives and lawyers of both parties will have another round of eloquence.

Eight hundred counterfeit banknotes of one yuan were taken back to the police station. The next day, they were sent to the Second Special Court for trial by Judge Li Changnian. Because the attorney of the Police Department requested detention and postponement of investigation, and to arrest and prosecute the accomplices at large, the court questioned Yao and ordered the defendant to be detained and rescheduled for further hearing on the 18th. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. It is now learned that on the day of this case's hearing, the detectives learned that the defendant's accomplices were hiding in a house at No. 159 Jiale Road. They rushed to the location and first arrested the landlord Ding Changhai (52 years old, from Anhui) and his wife Ding Fang (50 years old, from Hubei). They also arrested Zai Changheng (38 years old, from Jiangbei) and his mistress Xia Chen (30 years old, from Hanyang) in the storehouse. They found a package of counterfeit banknotes (the same style as the old version of the Bank of China previously seized) in the room, totaling 21, as well as a package of opium of various sizes, weighing more than ten taels, and a package of counterfeit lead double hao coins, totaling more than one hundred pieces. They were all taken to the police station for detention. Detectives were dispatched to guard the agency. Record of the Annual Meeting of the Architectural Society 127

The Chinese Architectural Society is the only architectural organization in the country. Established for more than ten years, its affairs have become increasingly developed. To date, it has more than sixty members. All well-known architects in the country are members of the society. In addition to researching architectural academics, they also contribute significantly to society and the architectural field. Every year, at the request of government offices or private individuals, they conduct inspections, audits, and mediate and arbitrate architectural cases, often reaching hundreds of cases, which shows the importance of the society to society. Every year at the end of the year, the society holds an annual meeting to conclude and report on the society's affairs for the year. The annual meeting was held on December 20th at the Guangdong Club. More than twenty architects attended, including Zhuang Jun, Li Jinpei, Xi Fuquan, Tong Jun, Dong Dayou, Zhao Shen, Wu Zhenying, Chen Zhi, and Yang Xiliu. After the formalities, Chairman Zhuang Jun reported on the society's activities for the year, followed by reports from the secretary, treasurer, and various committees on the work done this year. The following resolutions were then discussed and decided upon: The Architectural Regulations Nomenclature Committee proposed that standard formats be developed by the society for contract regulations and other documents used by architects, for use by members and non-members, in order to achieve uniformity, and that draft proposals be submitted to the General Assembly for approval. It was resolved to adopt the amendment. The proposed amendment to Article 9 of the Articles of Association was resolved to adopt the amendment. Regarding how to deal with members who have not paid their membership fees, it was resolved that the society should send a letter urging them to pay the outstanding fees within a limited time. Otherwise, they will be removed from the society and ordered to return their certificates. Regarding the economic and issue number issues of the publishing department, it was resolved that the board of directors should consult with the publishing committee to handle them. Regarding the issue of the existence of the society's offices, it was resolved that the society's office committee should consult with the administrative department to decide.

Manure Boat Capsizes in Chenjiazhui 131

Yesterday at 11:03 AM, a Chongming manure and ash boat owned by Cui Linjiang was sailing north in the river near Beichenjiazhui in Donggou, under sail. At that time, the No. 3 ferry, traveling from Shanghai to Wusong, passed by. It was parallel to the sailboat. The ferry sounded its horn as usual. Suddenly, the sailboat turned to the left and crossed the bow of the ferry. The ferry immediately stopped and reversed, but the sailboat's sail was caught by the wind and formed a T-shape with the ferry, causing it to collide and capsize. Amicable Settlement in the Case of Shanghai Art College Owing Rent 132

The Shanghai Art College's premises at 440 Caishi Road, French Concession, is the property of the Yongxi Hall of the Zheshao Guild Hall (commonly known as the Shaoxing Guild Hall) on Liyuan Road, Nanshi. The Shanghai Art College rented the premises for a monthly rent of 760 yuan, and a lease contract was signed. Recently, due to the Art College's accumulation of rent arrears that have not been cleared, the landlord, the Yongxi Hall of the Zheshao Guild Hall, through its legal representative Wei Hongwen, appointed lawyer Zheng Wentong as its agent and filed a lawsuit in the Civil Court of the Special No. 2 Court. According to the indictment, the defendant, Shanghai Art College, owed 2,815 yuan in rent before December 1933 and 11,400 yuan for fifteen months from October 1934 to December 1935, totaling 14,215 yuan. The plaintiff requested an investigation and prosecution, and because the defendant's movable property and school equipment were limited, the plaintiff requested permission for provisional execution and a judgment to terminate the lease, order the relocation and return of the premises, and bear the litigation costs. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Xiaoke heard the case in the Civil Court No. 7 based on the indictment. The plaintiff's lawyer appeared in court to state the reasons for the lawsuit and the objects of the judgment. The defendant, Shanghai Martial Arts College, sent a representative and its agent, lawyer Chen Tingrui, to appear in court. According to lawyer Chen's defense, the defendant first requested the rejection of the plaintiff's lawsuit and wanted to file a counterclaim. The reason was that the defendant did owe rent, but the facts were inconsistent. The premises rented by the defendant from the plaintiff were very large, and a part of them was sublet to others. In December 1934, due to carelessness, a part of the premises was destroyed by fire. The defendant immediately requested the plaintiff to rebuild them, but the plaintiff ignored the request. After the carelessness, the defendant lost a part of its income, amounting to two or three hundred gold. Now, the plaintiff wants to collect rent according to the original amount, but the defendant can only pay after the premises are rebuilt. Recently, Mr. Wang Xiaolai mediated and ordered the defendant to pay half of the rent arrears first, and the plaintiff would immediately rebuild the premises, as evidenced by a letter from the plaintiff, the Yongxi Hall of the Zheshao Guild Hall. The defendant would be able to pay half of the rent after school starts in March. Now it is the off-season, and there is no money to pay. However, the plaintiff disputed the defendant's willingness to pay half of the amount due to the distinction between old and new rent arrears. The court then persuaded both parties to reach a settlement, ordering the defendant to pay 8,000 yuan by the end of March. After receiving the payment, the plaintiff would immediately rebuild the premises. The defendant would pay half of the rent arrears when paying the new rent each month. If they failed to pay once, the entire amount would be executed. The plaintiff orally agreed to withdraw the request to terminate the lease and relocate. The minutes were recorded by both parties and signed before leaving the court.

Aunt Illegally Cashes Niece's Remittance 137

Tian Su'e, a woman from Hunan province, 22 years old, a student at a university in Shanghai, had been lodging at the home of her aunt, Madam Tian Huang (58 years old), at No. 284 Xinxin Lane, Rue du Père Robert, French Concession. Recently, Su'e moved to the Tianjitang Pharmacy at No. 226 Avenue du Grand Conseil. Su'e's mother in Hunan sent her 30 yuan for expenses through the post office on December 26 of last year. The post office delivered the letter to Tian Huang's address. Huang did not hand it over to Su'e, but secretly opened it. Seeing that there was a draft, she secretly used Su'e's seal, cashed the money from the post office, and spent it. Recently, Su'e received a letter from her mother at Tianjitang asking if she had received the money that was sent. Su'e asked her aunt about it, but Huang not only denied receiving the money but also made excuses to cover it up. Su'e then investigated with the post office and learned the whole story of her aunt's secret use of the seal and illegal cashing of the remittance. She reported it to the French Concession police. Wang Baoming, a detective, went and arrested Tian Huang and detained her. Yesterday morning, she was sent to the Criminal Court No. 8 of the Special No. 2 Court. Gu Shouxi, a lawyer from the police department, explained the case and requested an extension of the investigation before filing a lawsuit. Foreign Inspector of Customs Extorts; Demands 5,000 Yuan from Baoda Silk Company for Twelve Permits; Company Reports to Customs to Send Someone to Negotiate as Agreed; Police Prosecute for Abuse of Power and Accepting Bribes 138

Harrianter, a Western inspector of the Jianghai Customs in this city (claiming to be Swedish), went to the Baoda Silk Company at No. 284 Jiujiang Road and the warehouse at No. 11 Rue Amiral Bayle on the morning of January 9th to investigate permits. According to customs regulations, all permits for silk pieces that were sold out last year must be handed over to the customs inspector for reporting and cancellation by the end of this month to prevent the permits from being used to transport other goods to evade taxes. The reward for those who are fined is quite high. The Western officer found that the goods for twelve silk permits had been sold out for a long time and had not been reported. He extorted 5,000 yuan (according to customs regulations, goods that have been sold out and the permits exist, and are not used to transport other goods, are not fined). Sun Yueqing, a Yuyao native working at Beikaier Road, and manager Li of the company, discussed the matter and felt that the Western officer should not extort money. Sun informed Davis, the Western affairs manager, who in turn informed the tax commissioner and sent Qian Shiqing, a Chinese staff member. At approximately 3:00 PM that afternoon, Qian and Sun took 2,400 yuan in marked banknotes and went to Harrianter's house to negotiate. Harrianter agreed to accept 1,000 yuan, but the negotiations failed. Harrianter said that the company's twelve permits should have been reported earlier. According to customs regulations, a fine of 20,000 to 30,000 yuan would have to be paid. He had found a way to settle it for 5,000 yuan, which was very cheap. In the end, they paid him 2,400 yuan and agreed to pay the rest that night. Harrianter wrote down his home phone number and told them to call first when they sent the rest of the money. Sun and Qian both returned to the company and later took another 2,600 yuan in marked banknotes and delivered it to Harrianter. The next morning, Harrianter returned the twelve permits to the company. The day before yesterday, the police were informed and sent Chinese and Western detectives with a search warrant from the First Special District Court to arrest Harrianter at his address. They only found 90 yuan in unmarked banknotes in the iron box, but the original 5,000 yuan was not found. He was taken to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, he was sent to Criminal Court No. 3. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, explained the case and filed a public prosecution for abuse of power and accepting bribes. Davis, a Western customs officer, Qian Shiqing, a Chinese staff member, and Sun Yueqing, a customs broker from Baoda Silk Company, testified about the incident. When questioned, Harrianter said that he had been working at the customs for 22 years. When he went to the company's warehouse to investigate permits that day, he did not meet Mr. Sun. Mr. Sun personally came to his house with the twelve permits in question at 3:00 PM in the afternoon. He did not ask him for money. Moreover, he had already cancelled these permits with the customs. After cancellation according to regulations, they should be returned to the original owner. He worked diligently in the customs and was framed by Mr. Sun out of personal animosity. There was no extortion of 5,000 yuan. His pension for 22 years would be 40,000 to 50,000 yuan. He also hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him and requested to be released on bail. Judge Jiang Shuzhi ordered the defendant to be detained unless he could provide a 50,000 yuan guarantee. If he could not provide a guarantee, he would be detained. The sentence was scheduled to be announced next Monday.

Jin Ziming Sues Daughter-in-Law for Unchastity; Requests Severance of Family Relationship 139

Jin Ziming, a local resident living at No. 30 Kaiping Road, Yangjing Town, Pudong, and an employee of the Baidai Company, recently hired a lawyer to sue his daughter-in-law, Jin Jiang, in the local court for unchastity and adultery, and requested permission to sever family ties. Judge Chen Bingxin summoned both parties several times without a resolution. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Judge Chen specially opened the Fourth Court to continue the hearing. Both parties appeared in court with their lawyers. Jin Ziming testified that he was 64 years old. After his adopted son, Mingchang, died, he separated from his daughter-in-law, Jin Jiang, in June 1932 and gave her the three-story building on the rented nine acres of land to collect rent for a living. Originally, the rent was more than 90 yuan per month. In addition to the daughter-in-law's residence, there were still rooms for rent, which could earn her another 40 yuan per month. She (referring to Jin Jiang) became lascivious in her prosperity and committed adultery. On December 18 of last year, he caught her and handed her over to the police station to sever relations. The defendant, Jin Jiang, testified that she was 40 years old and a native of the area. She claimed that the plaintiff's testimony was completely inconsistent with the facts. She married the plaintiff's eldest son, Mingchang, in 1916. Unfortunately, her husband died of illness in 1921, leaving behind two sons who were still infants. She raised the orphans with hardship and perseverance for more than ten years. In 1932, the plaintiff suddenly had different intentions and separated from her without providing living expenses. She was forced to gather relatives and friends to negotiate with him. As a result, the plaintiff maintained the daily expenses of the daughter-in-law and orphans and signed a written agreement. The plaintiff voluntarily returned the clothing she had brought when she married and 700 yuan. As for the accusation of adultery, she was actually framed by the plaintiff. Fortunately, the police station investigated and released her. Now, the plaintiff intends to abandon her and disregard her, so she requests the judge to order the plaintiff to bear the living expenses of the mother and children for ten years from 1932 or pay 6,000 yuan in one lump sum. After hearing the testimony, the judge ordered the start of the debate, which was considered concluded, and scheduled the announcement of the verdict.

Russian Woman Dies Under Mysterious Circumstances; Forensic Examination 140

Maria Marakova, a Russian woman, 35 years old, and her husband, an Englishman named P吏司 (36 years old, an engineer at the Shanghai Electric Power Company), lived together in Apartment No. 1, Lane 750, Route Ghisi. The couple had been married for more than eight years. The night before last, they had a quarrel. Subsequently, the husband left in a huff, saying to his wife that he did not want to return. The wife ordered the servant Peng Wanyu to light the stove in her room for warmth. The next morning at 7:00 AM, Peng planned to go to the wife's bedroom to wait for instructions, but found the door tightly closed. He knocked but received no response. Peng did not suspect anything else and assumed that the wife was still asleep. At around 10:00 AM, the husband returned from outside and saw that the door had not been opened. He broke open the door and entered, only to find the wife naked and bloody, stiff on the bed. He reported it to the Hongkou Police Station, which dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the autopsy room on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Zhang Zongru of the First Special District Court, along with two forensic doctors, Wei and Zhang, and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the scene. After examining the body, the Chinese head constable Yin Xingsheng reported the previous situation. The husband, P吏司, and the sister of the deceased, Marakova, claimed that the cause of death was unknown and requested an autopsy. Mr. Zhang approved the request and ruled that the Russian woman, Maria Marakova, died under mysterious circumstances. Based on the request of the husband and sister for an autopsy, it should be approved to be handed over to the forensic doctor for autopsy, and the hearing was rescheduled.

Imposing upon Charitable Organizations to Defraud Wealth: Song Jusheng and Another Arrested 145

Song Jusheng, a native of Huzhou, residing at No. 13, Tongkang Lane, Mintiniyin Road in the French Concession, has no legitimate occupation. He specializes in impersonating charitable organizations to solicit donations. He previously impersonated the company commander of the First Company of the Special Service Battalion of the 78th Division of the National Revolutionary Army to solicit donations from all sectors of society. Recently, Zhang Zhen, a native of Jiangyin residing at No. 8, Tongkang Lane, suddenly told Song, "This approach of yours will not gain people's trust. It would be better to impersonate charitable enterprises." Thereupon, the two collaborated to print donation ledgers and stamps of the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Federation. Song then went out to solicit donations. On the 11th of the month, Song went to the home of Yang Zili at No. 3, Lane 272, Wuchang Road. He claimed that the organization was currently running a shelter in the Nanshi area and was short of funds. Therefore, he was specifically soliciting donations, requesting people to be charitable and contribute generously. He also presented a newspaper clipping about the shelter to gain trust. At the time, Yang suspected Song's behavior and asked about the details of the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Federation. Song's answers were vague. Yang realized it was an impersonation and summoned Detective Chen Xikang and Officer No. 1363 to arrest him and take him to the Hongkou Police Station. Zhang Zhen was subsequently apprehended. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Fifth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu prosecuted them for attempted fraud under Article 339, Section 2 of the Criminal Law. When questioned, the defendants confessed without hesitation. The police lawyer, having examined the circumstances of the case, believed that they had committed the crime of habitual fraud under Article 340 of the Criminal Law. Therefore, he amended the indictment. Furthermore, considering the crime of forging seals, the police were considering whether to add another charge. Therefore, he requested the court to grant an adjournment for the hearing. Zhan Liangce reviewed the report and ordered the case to be rescheduled for another hearing. The two defendants were remanded to custody.

After Expansion of Beds in Famous Hospitals, Addicts Eagerly Sent for Rehabilitation: As Many as Eighty-Six People Yesterday, Total Increase of Four Hundred and Thirty Beds 146

After the three municipal rehabilitation hospitals for addicts in South and North Shanghai expanded their beds and admitted addicts, it is now known that the Public Security Bureau has been sending addicts for rehabilitation as usual. The South and North Shanghai rehabilitation hospitals for addicts admitted seventy-two addicts in one day. The rehabilitation hospital for convicts also sent and transferred fourteen addicts for verification, a significant number. It is estimated that hundreds of addicts have yet to be sent for rehabilitation. After the expansion of each hospital, it should be sufficient to accommodate them. The original beds in each hospital totaled five hundred and fifty. Now, the total has increased to nine hundred and eighty, an increase of four hundred and thirty beds. Recent News from the Bank Committee 148

Since the Ministry of Finance implemented the unified currency system, domestic exchange rates have tended to be uniform. The Shanghai Banking Association subsequently proposed abolishing the affiliated Bank Market Committee. After several consultations among the banks, it was generally agreed that the establishment of the Market Committee was originally intended to provide member banks with opportunities to allocate exchange positions, connect with industry colleagues, and seek convenience in business handover through market meetings. It should not cease all secondary work simply because the domestic exchange market has been standardized by China's Central Bank. It is reported that the majority of banks have agreed, and the name of the association will remain. The daily market meeting will continue to be held at 9:00 AM as usual. However, future association affairs will focus on reporting interbank lending rates, silver coin imports and exports, domestic and foreign reserves, and investigating the profits and losses of the financial industry and the rise and fall of various industries. This will allow the banks in attendance to send staff to exchange and copy reports, thereby understanding financial trends and seeking mutual benefits for the industry.

Three months ago, an advertisement was placed in the newspaper soliciting designs for the clubhouse. Since the beginning of the solicitation, architects have flocked to the association to obtain regulations and maps. Many have been inquiring. The deadline for this solicitation is the 15th of this month. Architectural experts are submitting their completed designs. The association has been numbering them and issuing receipts. It is reported that the designs submitted are generally three-dimensional. After the deadline tomorrow (the 15th), it is planned to hire several architectural experts and convene the Construction Committee on the 18th to invite the experts to attend and review the designs submitted by the architects. The designs will be graded into three categories: A, B, and C. The first place design (A) will be chosen, and its architect will be hired by the association. Second place (B) will receive a prize of 500 yuan in legal tender. Third place (C) will receive a prize of 300 yuan in legal tender.
